<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/X_mark.svg/12px-X_mark.svg.png" width="12" height="14" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/X_mark.svg/18px-X_mark.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/X_mark.svg/24px-X_mark.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="525" data-file-height="600" /><span style="display:none">N</span>&#160;<span class="reflink plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Special:ComparePages&amp;rev1=477167117&amp;page2=Ethanol">verify</a></span>&#160;(<a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:WikiProject_Chemicals/Chembox_validation" title="Wikipedia:WikiProject Chemicals/Chembox validation">what is</a>&#160;<sup><img alt="Yes" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/7px-Yes_check.svg.png" width="7" height="7" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/11px-Yes_check.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fb/Yes_check.svg/14px-Yes_check.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600" /><span style="display:none">Y</span><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/X_mark.svg/7px-X_mark.svg.png" width="7" height="8" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/X_mark.svg/11px-X_mark.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/X_mark.svg/14px-X_mark.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="525" data-file-height="600" /><span style="display:none">N</span></sup>&#160;?)</td>

<tr style="background:#f8eaba; border-top:2px solid transparent;">
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;"><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Chemical_infobox#References" title="Wikipedia:Chemical infobox">Infobox&#160;references</a></td>
</tr>
<tr style="background:#f8eaba;">
<td style="width:40%; max-height:1px; border-top:2px solid transparent; border-right:1px solid transparent;"></td>
<td style="width:60%; max-height:1px; border-top:2px solid transparent; border-left:1px solid transparent;"></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p><b>Ethanol</b>, also called <b>alcohol</b>, <b>ethyl alcohol</b>, and <b>drinking alcohol</b>, is the principal type of <a href="/wiki/Alcohol" title="Alcohol">alcohol</a> found in <a href="/wiki/Alcoholic_beverages" class="mw-redirect" title="Alcoholic beverages">alcoholic beverages</a>. It is a <a href="/wiki/Volatility_(chemistry)" title="Volatility (chemistry)">volatile</a>, <a href="/wiki/Flammability" title="Flammability">flammable</a>, colorless liquid with a slight characteristic odor. Its chemical formula is <span class="chemf nowrap">C<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><br />
2</span>H<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><br />
6</span>O</span>, which can be written also as <span class="chemf nowrap">CH<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><br />
3</span></span>-<span class="chemf nowrap">CH<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><br />
2</span></span>-<span class="chemf nowrap">OH</span> or <span class="chemf nowrap">C<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><br />
2</span>H<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><br />
5</span></span>-<span class="chemf nowrap">OH</span> (an <a href="/wiki/Ethyl_group" title="Ethyl group">ethyl group</a> linked to a <a href="/wiki/Hydroxyl" class="mw-redirect" title="Hydroxyl">hydroxyl</a> group), and is often abbreviated as <b>EtOH</b>.</p>
<p>Ethanol is mostly produced by the <a href="/wiki/Fermentation" title="Fermentation">fermentation</a> of <a href="/wiki/Sugar" title="Sugar">sugars</a> by <a href="/wiki/Yeast" title="Yeast">yeasts</a>, or by <a href="/wiki/Petrochemistry" title="Petrochemistry">petrochemical</a> processes. It is an <a href="/wiki/Addiction" title="Addiction">addictive</a> <a href="/wiki/Psychoactive_drug" title="Psychoactive drug">psychoactive drug</a> (indeed one of the oldest and most common <a href="/wiki/Recreational_drug" class="mw-redirect" title="Recreational drug">recreational drugs</a>), causing a characteristic <a href="/wiki/Alcohol_intoxication" title="Alcohol intoxication">intoxication</a> ("drunkenness") and <a href="/wiki/Neurotoxic" class="mw-redirect" title="Neurotoxic">neurotoxicity</a> when consumed in sufficient quantities.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> It is widely used as a <a href="/wiki/Solvent" title="Solvent">solvent</a>, as <a href="/wiki/Alcohol_fuel" title="Alcohol fuel">fuel</a>, and as a <a href="/wiki/Feedstock" class="mw-redirect" title="Feedstock">feedstock</a> for <a href="/wiki/Chemical_synthesis" title="Chemical synthesis">synthesis</a> of other chemicals; as well as in many other minor uses.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ethanol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><i>Ethanol</i> is the <a href="/wiki/Systematic_name" title="Systematic name">systematic name</a> defined by the <a href="/wiki/IUPAC_nomenclature_of_organic_chemistry" title="IUPAC nomenclature of organic chemistry">International Union of Pure and Applied Chemistry (IUPAC)</a> for a compound consisting of <a href="/wiki/Alkyl_group" class="mw-redirect" title="Alkyl group">alkyl group</a> with two carbon <a href="/wiki/Atom" title="Atom">atoms</a> (prefix "eth-"), having a single bond between them (infix "-an-"), attached <a href="/wiki/Functional_group" title="Functional group">functional group</a>-OH group (suffix "-ol").<sup id="cite_ref-Pubchem_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pubchem-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p>The "eth-" prefix and the qualifier "ethyl" in "etyl alcohol" originally come from the name "ethyl" assigned in 1834 to the group <span class="chemf nowrap">C<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><br />
2</span>H<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><br />
5</span></span>- by <a href="/wiki/Justus_von_Liebig" title="Justus von Liebig">Justus Liebig</a>. He coined the word from the <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a> name <i>Aether</i> of the compound <span class="chemf nowrap">C<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><br />
2</span>H<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><br />
5</span></span>-O-<span class="chemf nowrap">C<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><br />
2</span>H<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><br />
5</span></span> (commonly called "ether" in <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a>, more specifically called "<a href="/wiki/Diethyl_ether" title="Diethyl ether">diethyl ether</a>").<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/Oxford_English_Dictionary" title="Oxford English Dictionary">Oxford English Dictionary</a>, <i>Ethyl</i> is a contraction of the Ancient Greek αἰθήρ (aithḗr, “upper air”) and the Greek word <i><span lang="grc">ύλη</span></i> (<i>hyle</i>, substance).<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p>The name <i>ethanol</i> was coined as a result of a resolution that was adopted at the International Conference on Chemical Nomenclature that was held in April 1892 in Geneva, Switzerland.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p>The term "<a href="/wiki/Alcohol" title="Alcohol">alcohol</a>" now refers to a wider class of substances in chemistry nomenclature, but in common parlance it remains the name of ethanol. The Oxford English Dictionary claims that it is a medieval loan from <a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Kohl_(cosmetics)" title="Kohl (cosmetics)">al-kuḥl</a></i>, a powdered ore of antimony used since aniquity as a cosmetic, and retained that meaning in <a href="/wiki/Middle_Latin" class="mw-redirect" title="Middle Latin">Middle Latin</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> The use of "alcohol" for ethanol (in full, "alcohol of wine") is modern, first recorded 1753, and by the later 17th century referred to "any sublimated substance; <a href="/wiki/Distilled_beverage" title="Distilled beverage">distilled spirit</a>" use for "the spirit of wine" (shortened from a full expression <i>alcohol of wine</i>). The systematic use in chemistry dates to 1850.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Uses">Uses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ethanol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Uses">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Medical">Medical</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ethanol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Medical">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Alcohol_(medical_use)" title="Alcohol (medical use)">Alcohol (medical use)</a></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Antiseptic">Antiseptic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ethanol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Antiseptic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Ethanol is used in medical wipes and most common antibacterial <a href="/wiki/Hand_sanitizer" title="Hand sanitizer">hand sanitizer</a> gels as an <a href="/wiki/Antiseptic" title="Antiseptic">antiseptic</a>. Ethanol kills organisms by <a href="/wiki/Denaturation_(biochemistry)" title="Denaturation (biochemistry)">denaturing</a> their <a href="/wiki/Protein" title="Protein">proteins</a> and dissolving their <a href="/wiki/Lipid" title="Lipid">lipids</a> and is effective against most <a href="/wiki/Bacteria" title="Bacteria">bacteria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fungus" title="Fungus">fungi</a>, and many <a href="/wiki/Virus" title="Virus">viruses</a>. However, ethanol is ineffective against bacterial <a href="/wiki/Endospore" title="Endospore">spores</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Antidote">Antidote</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ethanol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Antidote">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Ethanol may be administered as an <a href="/wiki/Antidote" title="Antidote">antidote</a> to <a href="/wiki/Methanol" title="Methanol">methanol</a><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Ethylene_glycol" title="Ethylene glycol">ethylene glycol</a> poisoning.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Medicinal_solvent">Medicinal solvent</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ethanol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Medicinal solvent">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Ethanol, often in high concentrations, is used to dissolve many water-insoluble medications and related compounds. Liquid preparations of cough and cold remedies, <a href="/wiki/Analgesics" class="mw-redirect" title="Analgesics">pain medication</a>, and mouth washes may be dissolved in 1 to 25% concentrations of ethanol and may need to be avoided in individuals with adverse reactions to ethanol such as <a href="/wiki/Alcohol-induced_respiratory_reactions" title="Alcohol-induced respiratory reactions">alcohol-induced respiratory reactions</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ann_Allergy_Asthma_Immunol_2013_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ann_Allergy_Asthma_Immunol_2013-23">[23]</a></sup> Ethanol is present in over 700 liquid medications including <a href="/wiki/Acetaminophen" class="mw-redirect" title="Acetaminophen">acetaminophen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iron_supplement" title="Iron supplement">iron supplements</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ranitidine" title="Ranitidine">ranitidine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Furosemide" title="Furosemide">furosemide</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mannitol" title="Mannitol">mannitol</a>, <a href="/wiki/Phenobarbital" title="Phenobarbital">phenobarbital</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trimethoprim/sulfamethoxazole" title="Trimethoprim/sulfamethoxazole">trimethoprim/sulfamethoxazole</a> and <a href="/wiki/Over-the-counter" class="mw-redirect" title="Over-the-counter">over-the-counter</a> <a href="/wiki/Cough_medicine" title="Cough medicine">cough medicine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Recreational">Recreational</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ethanol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Recreational">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Alcoholic_drink" title="Alcoholic drink">Alcoholic drink</a></div>
<p>As a <a href="/wiki/Central_nervous_system" title="Central nervous system">central nervous system</a> <a href="/wiki/Depressant" title="Depressant">depressant</a>, ethanol is one of the most commonly consumed <a href="/wiki/Psychoactive_drug" title="Psychoactive drug">psychoactive drugs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<p>The amount of ethanol in the body is typically quantified by <a href="/wiki/Blood_alcohol_content" title="Blood alcohol content">blood alcohol content</a> (BAC), which is here taken as weight of ethanol per unit volume of blood. Small doses of ethanol, in general, produce euphoria and relaxation; people experiencing these symptoms tend to become talkative and less inhibited, and may exhibit poor judgment. At higher dosages (BAC &gt; 1&#160;g/L), ethanol acts as a <a href="/wiki/Central_nervous_system" title="Central nervous system">central nervous system</a> <a href="/wiki/Depressant" title="Depressant">depressant</a>, producing at progressively higher dosages, impaired sensory and motor function, slowed cognition, stupefaction, unconsciousness, and possible death. Ethanol is commonly consumed as a recreational drug, especially while socializing, due to its psychoactive effects.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fuel">Fuel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ethanol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Fuel">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Engine_fuel">Engine fuel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ethanol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Engine fuel">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>

<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Ethanol_fuel" title="Ethanol fuel">Ethanol fuel</a></div>
<p>The largest single use of ethanol is as an engine <a href="/wiki/Fuel" title="Fuel">fuel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fuel_additive" class="mw-redirect" title="Fuel additive">fuel additive</a>. <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a> in particular relies heavily upon the use of ethanol as an engine fuel, due in part to its role as the globe's leading producer of ethanol.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Gasoline" title="Gasoline">Gasoline</a> sold in Brazil contains at least 25% <a href="/wiki/Anhydrous" title="Anhydrous">anhydrous</a> ethanol. Hydrous ethanol (about 95% ethanol and 5% water) can be used as fuel in more than 90% of new gasoline fueled cars sold in the country. Brazilian ethanol is produced from <a href="/wiki/Sugar_cane" class="mw-redirect" title="Sugar cane">sugar cane</a> and noted for high <a href="/wiki/Carbon_sequestration" title="Carbon sequestration">carbon sequestration</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-WaPo-Brazil_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WaPo-Brazil-31">[31]</a></sup> The US and many other countries primarily use E10 (10% ethanol, sometimes known as gasohol) and E85 (85% ethanol) ethanol/gasoline mixtures.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ethyl_alcohol_usp_grade.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Ethyl_alcohol_usp_grade.jpg/170px-Ethyl_alcohol_usp_grade.jpg" width="170" height="310" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Ethyl_alcohol_usp_grade.jpg/255px-Ethyl_alcohol_usp_grade.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Ethyl_alcohol_usp_grade.jpg/340px-Ethyl_alcohol_usp_grade.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1036" data-file-height="1892" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ethyl_alcohol_usp_grade.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/United_States_Pharmacopeia" title="United States Pharmacopeia">USP</a> grade ethanol for laboratory use.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Ethanol has been used as <a href="/wiki/Rocket_fuel" class="mw-redirect" title="Rocket fuel">rocket fuel</a> and is currently in <a href="/wiki/Light_aircraft" title="Light aircraft">lightweight</a> <a href="/wiki/Mark-III_X-racer" class="mw-redirect" title="Mark-III X-racer">rocket-powered racing aircraft</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-sdc20100426_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sdc20100426-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<p>Australian law limits the use of pure ethanol from sugarcane waste to 10% in automobiles. Older cars (and vintage cars designed to use a slower burning fuel) should have the engine valves upgraded or replaced.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to an industry <a href="/wiki/Advocacy_group" title="Advocacy group">advocacy group</a>, ethanol as a fuel reduces harmful <a href="/wiki/Motor_vehicle_emissions" class="mw-redirect" title="Motor vehicle emissions">tailpipe emissions</a> of carbon monoxide, particulate matter, <a href="/wiki/Oxides_of_nitrogen" class="mw-redirect" title="Oxides of nitrogen">oxides of nitrogen</a>, and other ozone-forming pollutants.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Argonne_National_Laboratory" title="Argonne National Laboratory">Argonne National Laboratory</a> analyzed greenhouse gas emissions of many different engine and fuel combinations, and found that <a href="/wiki/Biodiesel" title="Biodiesel">biodiesel</a>/petrodiesel blend (<a href="/wiki/B20_(biodiesel)" class="mw-redirect" title="B20 (biodiesel)">B20</a>) showed a reduction of 8%, conventional <a href="/wiki/E85" title="E85">E85</a> ethanol blend a reduction of 17% and <a href="/wiki/Cellulosic_ethanol" title="Cellulosic ethanol">cellulosic ethanol</a> 64%, compared with pure gasoline.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>Ethanol combustion in an internal combustion engine yields many of the products of incomplete combustion produced by gasoline and significantly larger amounts of <a href="/wiki/Formaldehyde" title="Formaldehyde">formaldehyde</a> and related species such as acetaldehyde.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> This leads to a significantly larger photochemical reactivity and more <a href="/wiki/Ground_level_ozone" class="mw-redirect" title="Ground level ozone">ground level ozone</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> These data have been assembled into <a href="/w/index.php?title=Clean_Fuels_Report&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Clean Fuels Report (page does not exist)">The Clean Fuels Report</a> comparison of fuel emissions<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> and show that ethanol exhaust generates 2.14&#160;times as much ozone as gasoline exhaust.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> When this is added into the custom <i>Localised Pollution Index (LPI)</i> of The Clean Fuels Report, the local pollution of ethanol (pollution that contributes to smog) is rated 1.7, where gasoline is 1.0 and higher numbers signify greater pollution.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The <a href="/wiki/California_Air_Resources_Board" title="California Air Resources Board">California Air Resources Board</a> formalized this issue in 2008 by recognizing control standards for formaldehydes as an emissions control group, much like the conventional <a href="/wiki/NOx" title="NOx">NOx</a> and Reactive Organic Gases (ROGs).<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<p>World production of ethanol in 2006 was 51 gigalitres (1.3<span style="margin:0 .15em 0 .25em">×</span>10<sup>10</sup>&#160;US&#160;gal), with 69% of the world supply coming from Brazil and the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> More than 20% of Brazilian cars are able to use 100% ethanol as fuel, which includes ethanol-only engines and <a href="/wiki/Flexible-fuel_vehicle" title="Flexible-fuel vehicle">flex-fuel</a> engines.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> Flex-fuel engines in Brazil are able to work with all ethanol, all gasoline or any mixture of both. In the US flex-fuel vehicles can run on 0% to 85% ethanol (15% gasoline) since higher ethanol blends are not yet allowed or efficient. Brazil supports this population of ethanol-burning automobiles with large national infrastructure that produces ethanol from domestically grown <a href="/wiki/Sugar_cane" class="mw-redirect" title="Sugar cane">sugar cane</a>. <a href="/wiki/Sugar_cane" class="mw-redirect" title="Sugar cane">Sugar cane</a> not only has a greater concentration of sucrose than corn (by about 30%), but is also much easier to extract. The <a href="/wiki/Bagasse" title="Bagasse">bagasse</a> generated by the process is not wasted, but is used in power plants to produce electricity.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In the United States, the ethanol fuel industry is based largely on <a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">corn</a>. According to the Renewable Fuels Association, as of 30 October 2007, 131 grain ethanol bio-refineries in the United States have the capacity to produce 7.0&#160;billion US gallons (26,000,000&#160;m<sup>3</sup>) of ethanol per year. An additional 72 construction projects underway (in the U.S.) can add 6.4&#160;billion US gallons (24,000,000&#160;m<sup>3</sup>) of new capacity in the next 18 months. Over time, it is believed that a material portion of the ≈150-billion-US-gallon (570,000,000&#160;m<sup>3</sup>) per year market for gasoline will begin to be replaced with fuel ethanol.<sup id="cite_ref-rfa1_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rfa1-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Sweet_sorghum" title="Sweet sorghum">Sweet sorghum</a> is another potential source of ethanol, and is suitable for growing in dryland conditions. The <a href="/wiki/International_Crops_Research_Institute_for_the_Semi-Arid_Tropics" title="International Crops Research Institute for the Semi-Arid Tropics">International Crops Research Institute for the Semi-Arid Tropics</a> (<a href="/wiki/ICRISAT" class="mw-redirect" title="ICRISAT">ICRISAT</a>) is investigating the possibility of growing sorgham as a source of fuel, food, and animal feed in arid parts of <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sweet_sorghum" title="Sweet sorghum">Sweet sorghum</a> has one-third the water requirement of sugarcane over the same time period. It also requires about 22% less water than corn (also known as maize). The world’s first sweet sorghum ethanol distillery began commercial production in 2007 in Andhra Pradesh, India.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<p>Ethanol's high <a href="/wiki/Miscibility" title="Miscibility">miscibility</a> with water makes it unsuitable for shipping through modern <a href="/wiki/Pipeline_transport" title="Pipeline transport">pipelines</a> like liquid hydrocarbons.<sup id="cite_ref-HornKrupp2009_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HornKrupp2009-45">[45]</a></sup> Mechanics have seen increased cases of damage to small engines (in particular, the <a href="/wiki/Carburetor" title="Carburetor">carburetor</a>) and attribute the damage to the increased water retention by ethanol in fuel.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tmulti tnone center">

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Rocket_fuel">Rocket fuel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ethanol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Rocket fuel">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Ethanol was commonly used as fuel in early <a href="/wiki/Bipropellant" class="mw-redirect" title="Bipropellant">bipropellant</a> <a href="/wiki/Rocket" title="Rocket">rocket</a> (liquid propelled) vehicles, in conjunction with an <a href="/wiki/Oxidizer" class="mw-redirect" title="Oxidizer">oxidizer</a> such as liquid oxygen. The German <a href="/wiki/V-2_rocket" title="V-2 rocket">V-2 rocket</a> of <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, credited with beginning the space age, used ethanol, mixed with 25% of water to reduce the combustion chamber temperature.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-braeunig_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-braeunig-48">[48]</a></sup> The V-2's design team helped develop U.S. rockets following World War II, including the ethanol-fueled <a href="/wiki/Redstone_(rocket)" class="mw-redirect" title="Redstone (rocket)">Redstone rocket</a> which launched the first U.S. satellite.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> Alcohols fell into general disuse as more efficient rocket fuels were developed.<sup id="cite_ref-braeunig_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-braeunig-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Fuel_cells">Fuel cells</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ethanol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Fuel cells">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Commercial fuel cells operate on reformed natural gas, <a href="/wiki/Hydrogen" title="Hydrogen">hydrogen</a> or <a href="/wiki/Methanol" title="Methanol">methanol</a>. Ethanol is an attractive alternative due to its wide availability, low cost, high purity and low toxicity. There are a wide range of fuel cell concepts that have been trialled including <a href="/wiki/Direct-ethanol_fuel_cell" title="Direct-ethanol fuel cell">direct-ethanol fuel cells</a>, auto-thermal reforming systems and thermally integrated systems. The majority of work is being conducted at a research level although there are a number of organizations at the beginning of commercialization of ethanol fuel cells.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Household_heating">Household heating</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ethanol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Household heating">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Ethanol fireplaces can be used for home heating or for decoration.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Feedstock">Feedstock</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ethanol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Feedstock">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="#Reactions">§&#160;Reactions</a></div>
<p>Ethanol is an important industrial ingredient. It has widespread use as a precursor for other organic compounds such as ethyl <a href="/wiki/Halide" title="Halide">halides</a>, ethyl <a href="/wiki/Ester" title="Ester">esters</a>, diethyl ether, acetic acid, and ethyl <a href="/wiki/Amine" title="Amine">amines</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Solvent">Solvent</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ethanol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Solvent">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Ethanol is <a href="/wiki/Miscible" class="mw-redirect" title="Miscible">miscible</a> with <a href="/wiki/Water_(molecule)" class="mw-redirect" title="Water (molecule)">water</a> and is a good general purpose <a href="/wiki/Solvent" title="Solvent">solvent</a>. It is found in <a href="/wiki/Paint" title="Paint">paints</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tincture" title="Tincture">tinctures</a>, markers, and personal care products such as mouthwashes, perfumes and deodorants. However, <a href="/wiki/Polysaccharides" class="mw-redirect" title="Polysaccharides">polysaccharides</a> <a href="/wiki/Ethanol_precipitation" title="Ethanol precipitation">precipitate</a> from aqueous solution in the presence of alcohol, and ethanol precipitation is used for this reason in the purification of <a href="/wiki/DNA" title="DNA">DNA</a> and <a href="/wiki/RNA" title="RNA">RNA</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Low-temperature_liquid">Low-temperature liquid</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ethanol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Low-temperature liquid">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Because of its low melting point (−114.14 °C) and low toxicity, ethanol is sometimes used in laboratories (with <a href="/wiki/Dry_ice" title="Dry ice">dry ice</a> or other coolants) as a <a href="/wiki/Cooling_bath" title="Cooling bath">cooling bath</a> to keep vessels at temperatures below the freezing point of water. For the same reason, it is also used as the active fluid in <a href="/wiki/Alcohol_thermometer" title="Alcohol thermometer">alcohol thermometers</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Adverse_effects">Adverse effects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ethanol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Adverse effects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Alcohol_and_health" title="Alcohol and health">Alcohol and health</a> and <a href="/wiki/Short-term_effects_of_alcohol" class="mw-redirect" title="Short-term effects of alcohol">Short-term effects of alcohol</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rational_harm_assessment_of_drugs_radar_plot.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Rational_harm_assessment_of_drugs_radar_plot.svg/220px-Rational_harm_assessment_of_drugs_radar_plot.svg.png" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Rational_harm_assessment_of_drugs_radar_plot.svg/330px-Rational_harm_assessment_of_drugs_radar_plot.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Rational_harm_assessment_of_drugs_radar_plot.svg/440px-Rational_harm_assessment_of_drugs_radar_plot.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="900" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rational_harm_assessment_of_drugs_radar_plot.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Addiction experts in psychiatry, chemistry, pharmacology, forensic science, epidemiology, and the police and legal services engaged in <a href="/wiki/Delphi_method" title="Delphi method">delphic analysis</a> regarding 20 popular recreational drugs. Alcohol was ranked 6th in dependence, 11th in physical harm, and 2nd in social harm.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Loss_of_balance">Loss of balance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ethanol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Loss of balance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>When alcohol reaches the brain, it has the ability to delay signals that are sent between nerve cells that control balance, thinking and movement.<sup id="cite_ref-body_alcohol_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-body_alcohol-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Gastrointestinal_diseases">Gastrointestinal diseases<span id="Gastrointestinal_disease"></span></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ethanol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Gastrointestinal diseases">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Stomach_mucosal_layer_labeled.svg" class="image"><img alt="compare" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Stomach_mucosal_layer_labeled.svg/200px-Stomach_mucosal_layer_labeled.svg.png" width="200" height="199" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Stomach_mucosal_layer_labeled.svg/300px-Stomach_mucosal_layer_labeled.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Stomach_mucosal_layer_labeled.svg/400px-Stomach_mucosal_layer_labeled.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="637" data-file-height="634" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Stomach_mucosal_layer_labeled.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Diagram of mucosal layer</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Alcohol stimulates gastric juice production, even when food is not present, and as a result, its consumption will stimulate acidic secretions normally intended to digest protein molecules. Consequently, the excess acidity may harm the inner lining of the stomach. The stomach lining is normally protected by a mucosal layer which prevents the stomach from essentially digesting itself. However, in patients who have a <a href="/wiki/Peptic_ulcer" title="Peptic ulcer">peptic ulcer</a> disease (PUD), this mucosal layer is broken down. PUD is commonly associated with the bacteria <i>H. pylori</i>. <i>H. pylori</i> secrete a toxin that weakens the mucosal wall, which as a result lead to acid and protein enzymes penetrating the weakened barrier. Because alcohol stimulates a person's stomach to secrete acid, a person with PUD should avoid drinking alcohol on an empty stomach. Drinking alcohol would cause more acid release which would further damage the already-weakened stomach wall.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> Complications of this disease could include a burning pain in the abdomen, bloating and in severe cases, the presence of dark black stools indicate internal bleeding.<sup id="cite_ref-PUD_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PUD-55">[55]</a></sup> A person who drinks alcohol regularly is strongly advised to reduce their intake to prevent PUD aggravation.<sup id="cite_ref-PUD_55-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PUD-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<p>Ingestion of alcohol can initiate systemic pro-inflammatory changes through two intestinal routes: (1) altering intestinal microbiota composition (dysbiosis), which increases lipopolysaccharide (LPS) release, and (2) degrading <a href="/wiki/Intestinal_mucosal_barrier" title="Intestinal mucosal barrier">intestinal mucosal barrier</a> integrity - thus allowing this (LPS) to enter the circulatory system. The major portion of the blood supply to the liver is provided by the portal vein. Therefore, while the liver is continuously fed nutrients from the intestine, it is also exposed to any bacteria and/or bacterial derivatives that breach the intestinal mucosal barrier. Consequently, LPS levels increase in the portal vein, liver and systemic circulation after alcohol intake. Immune cells in the liver respond to LPS with the production of reactive oxygen species (ROS), leukotrienes, chemokines and cytokines. These factors promote tissue inflammation and contribute to organ pathology.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Short-term_toxic_allergy-like_responses">Short-term toxic allergy-like responses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ethanol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Short-term toxic allergy-like responses">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Alcohol-induced_respiratory_reactions" title="Alcohol-induced respiratory reactions">Alcohol-induced respiratory reactions</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alcohol_flush_reaction" title="Alcohol flush reaction">Alcohol flush reaction</a></div>
<p>Ethanol-containing beverages can cause <a href="/wiki/Urticarial" class="mw-redirect" title="Urticarial">urticarial</a> skin eruptions, systemic <a href="/wiki/Dermatitis" title="Dermatitis">dermatitis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alcohol_flush_reaction" title="Alcohol flush reaction">alcohol flush reactions</a>, exacerbations of <a href="/wiki/Rhinitis" title="Rhinitis">rhinitis</a> and, more seriously and commonly, <a href="/wiki/Bronchoconstriction" title="Bronchoconstriction">bronchoconstriction</a> in patients with a history of <a href="/wiki/Asthma" title="Asthma">asthma</a>. These reactions occur within 1–60 minutes of ethanol ingestion and are due to: <b>1)</b> genetic abnormalities in the metabolism of ethanol which cause the ethanol metabolite, <a href="/wiki/Acetaldehyde" title="Acetaldehyde">acetaldehyde</a>, to accumulate in tissues and trigger the release of <a href="/wiki/Histamine" title="Histamine">histamine</a>, the evoker of these symptoms; <b>2)</b> true <a href="/wiki/Allergy" title="Allergy">allergy</a> reactions to <a href="/wiki/Allergens" class="mw-redirect" title="Allergens">allergens</a> occurring naturally in, or contaminating, alcoholic beverages, particularly wines and beers, and <b>3)</b> unknown causes.<sup id="cite_ref-Ann_Allergy_Asthma_Immunol_2013_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ann_Allergy_Asthma_Immunol_2013-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Long-term">Long-term</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ethanol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Long-term">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Long-term_effects_of_alcohol" class="mw-redirect" title="Long-term effects of alcohol">Long-term effects of alcohol</a></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Birth_defects">Birth defects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ethanol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Birth defects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Fetal_alcohol_syndrome" class="mw-redirect" title="Fetal alcohol syndrome">fetal alcohol syndrome</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fetal_alcohol_spectrum_disorder" title="Fetal alcohol spectrum disorder">fetal alcohol spectrum disorder</a></div>
<p>Ethanol is classified as a <a href="/wiki/Teratogen" class="mw-redirect" title="Teratogen">teratogen</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Identifying_reliable_sources_(medicine)" title="Wikipedia:Identifying reliable sources (medicine)"><span title="Material near this tag needs references to reliable medical sources. (February 2016)">medical citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> According to the CDC, alcohol consumption by women of child-bearing age who are not using birth control increases the risk of fetal alcohol syndrome. The CDC currently recommends complete abstinence from alcoholic beverages.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Cancer">Cancer</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ethanol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Cancer">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/International_Agency_for_Research_on_Cancer" title="International Agency for Research on Cancer">IARC</a> list ethanol in alcoholic beverages as <i>Group 1 carcinogens</i> and arguments "There is sufficient evidence for the <a href="/wiki/Alcohol_and_cancer" title="Alcohol and cancer">carcinogenicity</a> of <a href="/wiki/Acetaldehyde" title="Acetaldehyde">acetaldehyde</a> (the major metabolite of ethanol) in experimental animals."<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_effects">Other effects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ethanol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Other effects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Frequent drinking of alcoholic beverages has been shown to be a major contributing factor in cases of elevated blood levels of <a href="/wiki/Triglyceride" title="Triglyceride">triglycerides</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Reinforcement_disorders">Reinforcement disorders</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ethanol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Reinforcement disorders">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Addiction">Addiction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ethanol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Addiction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Alcoholism" title="Alcoholism">Alcoholism</a></div>
<p>The reinforcing effects of alcohol consumption are mediated by <a href="/wiki/Acetaldehyde" title="Acetaldehyde">acetaldehyde</a> generated by <a href="/wiki/Catalase" title="Catalase">catalase</a> and other oxidizing enzymes such as <a href="/wiki/CYP2E1" title="CYP2E1">cytochrome P-4502E1</a> in the brain.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> Although acetaldehyde has been associated with some of the adverse and toxic effects of ethanol, it appears to play a central role in the activation of the <a href="/wiki/Mesolimbic_pathway" title="Mesolimbic pathway">mesolimbic dopamine system</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Mesolimbic_dopamine_release_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mesolimbic_dopamine_release-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<p>Ethanol's rewarding and reinforcing (i.e., <a href="/wiki/Addictive" class="mw-redirect" title="Addictive">addictive</a>) properties are mediated through its effects on <a href="/wiki/Dopamine" title="Dopamine">dopamine</a> neurons in the <a href="/wiki/Mesolimbic_reward_pathway" class="mw-redirect" title="Mesolimbic reward pathway">mesolimbic reward pathway</a>, which connects the <a href="/wiki/Ventral_tegmental_area" title="Ventral tegmental area">ventral tegmental area</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Nucleus_accumbens" title="Nucleus accumbens">nucleus accumbens</a> (NAcc).<sup id="cite_ref-Alcoholism_.CE.94FosB_DB_entry_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Alcoholism_.CE.94FosB_DB_entry-62">[62]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Alcoholism_.CE.94FosB_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Alcoholism_.CE.94FosB-63">[63]</a></sup> One of ethanol's primary effects is the allosteric inhibition of <a href="/wiki/NMDA_receptor" title="NMDA receptor">NMDA receptors</a> and facilitation of <a href="/wiki/GABAA_receptor" title="GABAA receptor">GABA<sub>A</sub> receptors</a> (e.g., enhanced GABA<sub>A</sub> receptor-mediated <a href="/wiki/Chloride" title="Chloride">chloride</a> flux through <a href="/wiki/Allosteric_regulation" title="Allosteric regulation">allosteric regulation</a> of the receptor).<sup id="cite_ref-NHM-Ethanol_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NHM-Ethanol-64">[64]</a></sup> At high doses, ethanol inhibits most <a href="/wiki/Ligand_gated_ion_channel" class="mw-redirect" title="Ligand gated ion channel">ligand gated ion channels</a> and <a href="/wiki/Voltage_gated_ion_channel" class="mw-redirect" title="Voltage gated ion channel">voltage gated ion channels</a> in neurons as well.<sup id="cite_ref-NHM-Ethanol_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NHM-Ethanol-64">[64]</a></sup></p>
<p>With acute alcohol consumption, <a href="/wiki/Dopamine" title="Dopamine">dopamine</a> is released in the <a href="/wiki/Chemical_synapse" title="Chemical synapse">synapses</a> of the mesolimbic pathway, in turn heightening activation of postsynaptic <a href="/wiki/Dopamine_receptor_D1" title="Dopamine receptor D1">D1 receptors</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Alcoholism_.CE.94FosB_DB_entry_62-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Alcoholism_.CE.94FosB_DB_entry-62">[62]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Alcoholism_.CE.94FosB_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Alcoholism_.CE.94FosB-63">[63]</a></sup> The activation of these receptors triggers postsynaptic internal signaling events through <a href="/wiki/Protein_kinase_A" title="Protein kinase A">protein kinase A</a> which ultimately <a href="/wiki/Phosphorylate" class="mw-redirect" title="Phosphorylate">phosphorylate</a> <a href="/wiki/CAMP_response_element_binding_protein" class="mw-redirect" title="CAMP response element binding protein">cAMP response element binding protein</a> (CREB), inducing CREB-mediated changes in <a href="/wiki/Gene_expression" title="Gene expression">gene expression</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Alcoholism_.CE.94FosB_DB_entry_62-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Alcoholism_.CE.94FosB_DB_entry-62">[62]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Alcoholism_.CE.94FosB_63-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Alcoholism_.CE.94FosB-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<p>With chronic alcohol intake, consumption of ethanol similarly induces CREB phosphorylation through the D1 receptor pathway, but it also alters <a href="/wiki/NMDA_receptor" title="NMDA receptor">NMDA receptor</a> function through phosphorylation mechanisms;<sup id="cite_ref-Alcoholism_.CE.94FosB_DB_entry_62-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Alcoholism_.CE.94FosB_DB_entry-62">[62]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Alcoholism_.CE.94FosB_63-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Alcoholism_.CE.94FosB-63">[63]</a></sup> an adaptive <a href="/wiki/Downregulation_and_upregulation" title="Downregulation and upregulation">downregulation</a> of the D1 receptor pathway and CREB function occurs as well.<sup id="cite_ref-Alcoholism_.CE.94FosB_DB_entry_62-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Alcoholism_.CE.94FosB_DB_entry-62">[62]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Alcoholism_.CE.94FosB_63-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Alcoholism_.CE.94FosB-63">[63]</a></sup> Chronic consumption is also associated with an effect on CREB phosphorylation and function via postsynaptic NMDA receptor signaling cascades through a <a href="/wiki/MAPK/ERK_pathway" title="MAPK/ERK pathway">MAPK/ERK pathway</a> and <a href="/wiki/CAMK" title="CAMK">CAMK</a>-mediated pathway.<sup id="cite_ref-Alcoholism_.CE.94FosB_63-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Alcoholism_.CE.94FosB-63">[63]</a></sup> These modifications to CREB function in the mesolimbic pathway <a href="/wiki/Inducible_gene" class="mw-redirect" title="Inducible gene">induce expression</a> (i.e., increase gene expression) of ΔFosB in the <abbr title="nucleus accumbens">NAcc</abbr>,<sup id="cite_ref-Alcoholism_.CE.94FosB_63-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Alcoholism_.CE.94FosB-63">[63]</a></sup> where ΔFosB is the "master control protein" that, when overexpressed in the NAcc, is <a href="/wiki/Necessary_and_sufficient" class="mw-redirect" title="Necessary and sufficient">necessary and sufficient</a> for the development and maintenance of an addictive state (i.e., its overexpression in the nucleus accumbens produces and then directly modulates compulsive alcohol consumption).<sup id="cite_ref-Alcoholism_.CE.94FosB_63-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Alcoholism_.CE.94FosB-63">[63]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-What_the_.CE.94FosB.3F_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-What_the_.CE.94FosB.3F-65">[65]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Cellular_basis_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cellular_basis-66">[66]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Nestler_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nestler-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Dependence_and_withdrawal">Dependence and withdrawal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ethanol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Dependence and withdrawal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Alcohol_withdrawal_syndrome" title="Alcohol withdrawal syndrome">Alcohol withdrawal syndrome</a></div>
<p>Discontinuing consumption of alcohol after several years of heavy drinking can also be fatal. Alcohol withdrawal can cause anxiety, autonomic dysfunction, seizures, and hallucinations. <a href="/wiki/Delirium_tremens" title="Delirium tremens">Delirium tremens</a> is a condition that requires people with a long history of heavy drinking to undertake an <a href="/wiki/Alcohol_detoxification" title="Alcohol detoxification">alcohol detoxification</a> regimen.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Overdose">Overdose</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ethanol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Overdose">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Alcohol_consumption_and_health" class="mw-redirect" title="Alcohol consumption and health">Alcohol consumption and health</a></div>
<table class="wikitable" style="float:right; width:25em; margin-left: 1em">
<tr>
<th>BAC (g/L)</th>
<th>BAC<br />

<th>Symptoms<sup id="cite_ref-Pohorecky_.26_Brick_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pohorecky_.26_Brick-68">[68]</a></sup></th>

<tr>

<tr>

</tr>
<tr>
<td>&gt;5.5</td>
